I'm setting up an etsy store that is focused on Funny dnd shirts primarily for gen x men. I'm going to upload some designs and I need you to help come up with a good store name on etsy that will help start brand building and be good SEO with my target audience

## ChatGPT

I think you've picked a **great niche**. Looking at the designs, I notice a few things:

- They're not "high fantasy" serious—they're **funny, slightly unhinged, meme-style D&D humor.**
- The artwork is bold and colorful, which appeals more to **35-55 year old Gen X gamers** than minimalist designs.
- The humor is the kind someone who's been playing since AD&D or 3.5 would appreciate.
- These feel like shirts someone wears to game night, conventions, breweries, or as gifts.

Because of that, I would **not** make the store too generic like "Fantasy Shirts." I'd build a brand that people remember.

## What your Etsy name should accomplish

Ideally it should:

- Mention a gaming keyword (Dungeon, Dice, Crit, Roll, Tavern, Quest, Loot)
- Be memorable
- Expand beyond shirts (hoodies, mugs, stickers, dice trays later)
- Feel like a real brand rather than an SEO keyword dump

# Etsy SEO Strategy

One thing many Etsy sellers miss is that **your shop name is only a small SEO factor**. Your listings matter much more.

Instead, use a memorable shop name and optimize every listing title.

For example:

> Funny DnD Shirt | Beholder Crit Fail | Tabletop RPG Gift | Dungeon Master Shirt | D20 Meme Tee | Fantasy Gaming Gift

This gives Etsy's algorithm the keywords it needs while your brand stays memorable.

---

# My Favorite for Your Style

Based on the designs you shared, your humor feels like:

- Old-school D&D
- Gen X sarcasm
- Critical fails
- Chaotic game nights
- Inside jokes
- Beer-and-pretzels tabletop gaming

I'd build the entire brand around that vibe.

### Brand Recommendation

**Crit Happens Co.**

Tagline ideas:

- *Rolled Low. Laughed Hard.*
- *Critical Fails Since Forever.*
- *Wear Your Worst Roll.*
- *Game Night Gear for Legendary Disasters.*
- *Natural 1. Legendary Story.*

It has the feel of a brand someone might recognize at a convention or on social media, and it leaves plenty of room to expand into mugs, dice bags, stickers, hoodies, and other tabletop gaming merchandise.

## User

how can I make sure I'm not sued if I use crit happens Co. Can I also drop the CO? I don't like it, what service does it perform?

## ChatGPT

You can absolutely drop the "Co." There is no legal requirement or SEO benefit to having it.

**"Crit Happens"** is cleaner, shorter, and more memorable than **"Crit Happens Co."**

The reason people add "Co.", "Studio", "Supply", "Works", etc. is usually because:

1. The plain name is already taken on Etsy.
2. The domain name is unavailable.
3. It makes the brand feel more established.

Examples:
- Crit Happens
- Crit Happens Studio
- Crit Happens Workshop
- Crit Happens Supply
- Crit Happens Designs

Personally, I'd prefer **Crit Happens** if it's available.

---

## The bigger issue: can someone sue you?

Anyone can sue anyone, but what you're really asking is:

**"Could I be forced to stop using the name because it infringes a trademark?"**

Possibly.

"Crit Happens" is a fairly obvious gaming pun, which means there's a decent chance somebody has already used or trademarked it for gaming merchandise.

Before investing in branding, you should check:

### 1. USPTO Trademark (most important)

:

- Crit Happens
- Crit Happen
- Crit Happens Apparel
- Crit Happens Clothing

at:

[USPTO Trademark ](https://tm.uspto.gov/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

Look specifically for:
- Clothing
- Apparel
- T-shirts
- Merchandise
- Gaming merchandise

---

### 2. Etsy 

 Etsy for:

- Crit Happens
- Crit Happens shirt
- Crit Happens apparel

If you find dozens of established shops using it, that's a warning sign even if no trademark exists.

---

### 3. Domain 

Check whether:

- crithappens.com
- crithappens.ca
- crithappensshop.com

are available.

If you eventually want a standalone website, this matters.

---

## A branding mistake I see all the time

Many new Etsy sellers choose names that are:

- Clever
- Memorable

but also

- Used by 50 other gaming businesses

That creates problems later.

---

## Names I'd actually consider safer

Instead of a common D&D pun, create something slightly more unique.

Examples:

- Dungeon Dad
- Roll Wrong
- Tavern Loot
- Side Quest Supply
- Natural One Society
- Failed Saving Throw
- Dice & Dysfunction
- The Last Hit Point
- Miscast Magic
- Initiative Zero

These are less likely to already be heavily claimed.

---

## What I would do before opening the shop

1. Etsy.
2. Google.
3. the USPTO database.
4. Check domain availability.
5. Check Instagram, Facebook, and TikTok handles.

If all five are reasonably clean, then proceed.

For a long-term brand, I'd actually be more exd about a name like **Dungeon Dad**, **Roll Wrong**, or **The Last Hit Point** because they're more distinctive and easier to own than a common phrase like "Crit Happens."

If you want, I can brainstorm **50 Etsy shop names specifically optimized for Gen X D&D humor brands that are likely to have lower trademark conflict risk and stronger domain availability prospects.**

I did some initial ing, and I would **not build your brand around "Crit Happens."**

Here's why:

### 1. The phrase is already everywhere

There are large numbers of Etsy listings using "Crit Happens" on shirts, mugs, stickers, hats, dice trays, signs, and other RPG merchandise. ([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/ca/market/crit_happens?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

There are also independent shirt designs on TeePublic, Amazon, and other apparel marketplaces that have been around for years. ([TeePublic](https://www.teepublic.com/t-shirt/1040869-crit-happens?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### 2. Brand confusion is likely

I also found:
- A D&D podcast called "When Crit Happens." ([When Crit Happens](https://whencrithappens.com/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))
- Various gaming-related products and content using the phrase. ([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/ca/market/crit_happens?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

Even if you could legally use it, you'd be competing with years of existing usage.

### 3. I could not verify trademark safety

I was able to confirm the USPTO resources, but I could not reliably retrieve an authoritative trademark record for "Crit Happens" itself from results. ([USPTO](https://www.uspto.gov/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

For a real clearance check before investing money, I'd still recommend:
- USPTO trademark 
- Canadian trademark database 
- Domain 
- Etsy shop name 

A trademark attorney would be needed for a definitive opinion.

## User

I like Dungeon Dad - can you do es on that for good SEO, make sure it's good for etsy instagram tiktok youtube, and not claimed on USPTO database

## ChatGPT

I would **not use "Dungeon Dad" as your Etsy store brand name**.

After ing, the issue isn't SEO—it's **brand ownership and differentiation**.

### What I found

**Etsy**
- There are already many "Dungeon Dad" shirts, SVGs, mugs, and Father's Day products on Etsy. The phrase is heavily used as a product keyword. ([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/market/dungeon_dad_t_shirt?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

**YouTube**
- There is an established D&D creator using the brand **Dungeon Dad** with over 200K subscribers. ([youtube.com](https://www.youtube.com/c/dungeondad?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

**Patreon**
- The same creator operates a substantial Patreon under the Dungeon Dad name. ([Patreon](https://www.patreon.com/DungeonDad?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

**Instagram**
- There are existing Dungeon Dad accounts already active in the tabletop gaming space. ([Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/the_dungeon_dad/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

**Facebook**
- There is an established Dungeon Dad gaming presence there as well. ([Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/DungeonDad/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### SEO Analysis

The good news:
- "Dungeon Dad" is a phrase buyers already for. ([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/market/dungeon_dad_t_shirt?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

The bad news:
- Because it is already heavily associated with existing products and creators, building a unique brand around it would be difficult. People ing "Dungeon Dad" may be looking for shirts, a YouTube creator, social accounts, or other existing products. ([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/market/dungeon_dad_t_shirt?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### USPTO

I was not able to perform a definitive trademark clearance from the trademark database itself, so I cannot tell you that it is legally clear.

However, even if there were no active trademark, I'd still avoid it because:
- Established creator already using the name
- Existing social handles
- Existing Etsy ecosystem around the phrase
- Difficult to rank your own website later

### What I would do instead

Take the *idea* of Dungeon Dad and make it uniquely yours.

Examples:

- Dungeon Dad HQ
- Dungeon Dad Life
- Dungeon Dad Workshop
- Dungeon Dad Tavern
- Dungeon Dad & Co
- The Dice Dad
- Roll Wrong
- Last Hit Point
- Failed Saving Throw
- Tavern Loot
- Natural One Society
- Side Quest Syndicate

Of those, **Roll Wrong** stands out because it matches your artwork perfectly:
- Beholder crit fails
- Party wipes
- Bad rolls
- Funny disasters
- Gen X sarcasm

It's also much more likely to have available branding across Etsy, Instagram, TikTok, YouTube, and a future website.

My recommendation based on what I found:

| Name | SEO | Brandability | Conflict Risk |
|--------|--------|--------|--------|
| Dungeon Dad | A+ | C | High |
| Crit Happens | A | B | High |
| Roll Wrong | B+ | A+ | Low |
| Last Hit Point | B | A | Low |
| Failed Saving Throw | B+ | A | Low |
| Tavern Loot | B | A | Low |

If you're serious about building a long-term Etsy brand rather than just opening a store, I'd spend the time finding a name that's **90% as catchy as Dungeon Dad but 10x easier to own**. My current favorite for your designs is **Roll Wrong**.

### Why I like Side Quest Syndicate

Your designs aren't really about being a dad.

They're about:

- Crit fails
- Bad decisions
- Party chaos
- Funny encounters
- Campaign disasters
- Tabletop humor

"Side Quest Syndicate" captures that much better.

It feels like:

> "A secret society of gamers who constantly get distracted and make terrible decisions."

That's actually the emotional vibe of your designs.

---

### SEO Reality

A lot of Etsy sellers overestimate the importance of the shop name.

Your traffic will come from listing titles like:

- Funny DnD Shirt
- Beholder Shirt
- Dungeon Master Gift
- D20 Meme Shirt
- Critical Fail Tee
- RPG Gamer Gift

not from the store name itself.

So I'd choose the strongest brand and let the listings handle SEO.

---

### Potential Issue

The only thing I'd watch is that **"Side Quest"** is used everywhere in gaming.

Not necessarily trademarked for apparel, but it's a very common gaming phrase.

The addition of **"Syndicate"** helps a lot because the full phrase becomes much more distinctive.

For the style of artwork you've shown, Side Quest Syndicate is closer to a lifestyle brand and gives you room to expand into hundreds of designs without being trapped by one joke or demographic.

## The Side Quest Society — Brand Risk Assessment

### Etsy: 🟢 Good

I found lots of products using the phrase "side quest" (which is unavoidable), but not a dominant apparel brand with your exact name.([Etsy](https://www.etsy.com/ca/market/side_quest_t_shirt?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

**Verdict:** Good.

---

### Instagram: 🟡 Moderate Conflict

There are existing accounts using very similar names:

- "The Side Quest Society HQ" appears active([Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/thesidequestsocietyhq/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))4
- "SideQuestSociety" also exists([Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/sidequestsoc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))9

These are relatively small accounts, not major brands.

**Verdict:** Not a deal-breaker, but getting your exact preferred handle may be difficult.

Possible handles:

- @TheSideQuestSocietyOfficial
- @SideQuestSocietyShop
- @JoinTheSideQuestSociety
- @TheSQSociety

---

### YouTube: 🟡 Moderate Conflict

There is a small YouTube channel named "Side Quest Society([YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCIoTnGMIilP7AmlRafomKmA?utm_source=chatgpt.com))24

It's not a major creator, but it means the exact channel name may already be taken.

**Verdict:** Mild concern.

---

### TikTok: 🟢 Probably Fine

I didn't find evidence of a large gaming brand owning "The Side Quest Society."

You'd still need to claim handles immediately if you move forward.

**Verdict:** Good.

---

### Trademark Risk: 🟡 Unknown / Probably Manageable

I did not find evidence that **"The Side Quest Society"** itself is a major trademarked apparel brand.

However, "Side Quest" is used everywhere:

- Side Quest VR
- Side Quest gaming businesses
- Side Quest merchandise
- Side Quest apparel products
- Side Quest Cards & Games busine([SideQuest](https://sidequestvr.com/terms?utm_source=chatgpt.com))ch13

The risk isn't the full phrase.

The risk is that the **"Side Quest"** portion is heavily used.

Before spending money on logos, packaging, or a website, I'd still run:
- Canadian trademark database
- USPTO TESS 
- WIPO 

for the exact phrase.

# My Strategic Take

The biggest issue isn't legal risk.

It's **discoverability**.

If someone hears:

> "Check out The Side Quest Society"

they'll likely remember it.

If someone es:

> side quest society

they'll compete with:
- gaming channels
- D&D modules
- social accounts
- general side-quest con([Foundry Virtual Tabletop](https://foundryvtt.com/packages/side-quest-society-free?utm_source=chatgpt.com))ch24

---

**My confidence in recommending it: High, with one caveat**

The caveat: **“Poor Decisions” is already used in apparel**, and I found a USPTO-related listing for **POOR DECISIONS ALUMNI** covering clothing, including shirts, hoodies, hats, and other apparel. That does not automatically block you, but it is the main thing I would have a trademark attorney look at before filing or investing heavily. ([USPTO Report](https://uspto.report/TM/99794997?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

## What I found

| Area | Result | Risk |
|---|---:|---:|
| Etsy shop name | No obvious exact-shop conflict found | Low |
| Etsy listings | “Poor decisions” appears in mug/shirt-style products, but not exact brand dominance | Medium-low |
| Instagram | Phrase appears in posts, mostly nightlife/bar/event content; no obvious dominant D&D apparel brand found | Medium-low |
| TikTok | Could not directly verify handle availability; no strong indexed conflict found | Unknown/medium-low |
| YouTube | No obvious channel owning exact phrase as a brand | Low |
| Domains | No clear indexed active exact domain found for the full phrase | Medium-low, verify manually |
| USPTO/trademark | No exact “The League of Poor Decisions” hit found in indexed results, but **POOR DECISIONS ALUMNI** exists for apparel | Medium |

## The good news

**The exact phrase appears much less crowded than “Dungeon Dad,” “Crit Happens,” or “The Side Quest Society.”** results mostly reed casual uses, fantasy football league names, bar/event marketing, Reddit mentions, and generic “poor decisions” jokes rather than a major tabletop/apparel brand. ([Reddit](https://www.reddit.com/r/YahooFantasy/comments/163iztm/league_recruitment_weekly_thread/?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

That is exactly what you want: some phrase familiarity, but not a dominant competitor.

## The biggest concern

The closest meaningful conflict I found is **POOR DECISIONS ALUMNI**, which is tied to clothing goods. Because your shop would also sell apparel, this is the one risk I would not ignore. ([USPTO Report](https://uspto.report/TM/99794997?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

That said, your full phrase **The League of Poor Decisions** is much more distinctive than just **Poor Decisions**, and the tabletop/fantasy positioning helps differentiate it.

## Copyright vs trademark

Copyright is probably not your main issue here. Short phrases and business names are generally not protected by copyright. The real issue is **trademark**, meaning whether buyers might confuse your brand with another apparel brand.

## User

I'm not canadian or in canada. I'm in Florida and a us zen. Does that matter with copywrite?

## ChatGPT

Yes, it matters—but not in the way most Etsy sellers think.

First, a terminology point:

- **Copyright** protects artwork, illustrations, text, logos, and creative works.
- **Trademark** protects brand names, business names, slogans, and logos used in commerce.

For your Etsy shop name, you're almost entirely dealing with **trademark**, not copyright.

### Since you're in Florida and selling in the U.S.

The databases that matter most are:

1. **USPTO federal trademark database** (most important)
2. Existing use in commerce within the U.S.
3. Etsy marketplace usage
4. Domain ownership
5. Social handle ownership

Canadian trademark registrations generally won't stop you from operating in the U.S. unless that company is also doing business here or has U.S. trademark rights.

### Phase 1: Claim the brand

Before spending money on logos:

- Etsy shop
- Instagram
- TikTok
- YouTube
- Facebook page
- Domain

all on the same day.

If you can't get consistent branding, that's a warning sign.

Example:

Good:
- @leagueofpoordecisions everywhere
- leagueofpoordecisions.com

Bad:
- Etsy: LeagueOfPoorDecisions
- Instagram: LeagueOfPoorDecisionsOfficial247
- TikTok: LeaguePoorDecisionsStore

 for:

- League of Poor Decisions
- Poor Decisions
- Poor Decision
- League of Bad Decisions
- Similar apparel marks

The question isn't:

> "Is there an exact match?"

The question is:

> "Would consumers think these brands are related?"

That's the trademark test.

## User

can i by shop name on etsy?

## ChatGPT

Yes. Etsy doesn't have a perfect "shop name availability checker," but there are several ways to by shop name.

### Fastest Method

In Google, :

```text
site:etsy.com/shop "The Natural One Society"
```

or

```text
site:etsy.com/shop "League of Poor Decisions"
```

If an Etsy shop exists with that exact name, Google will often find it.

---

### Direct Etsy URL Test

Try:

```text
https://www.etsy.com/shop/TheNaturalOneSociety
```

and

```text
https://www.etsy.com/shop/LeagueOfPoorDecisions
```

If the shop exists, Etsy will load it.

If not, you'll typically get a "Sorry, this shop doesn't exist" message.

---

### Etsy Bar

 for:

```text
The Natural One Society
```

Then filter mentally:

- Shops
- Listings
- Store names appearing under listings

The problem is Etsy's favors products, not shop names.

---

### What I Would Actually Do

For any finalist name, run these checks:

#### Etsy
- Exact shop name
- Similar shop names
- Product listings using the phrase

#### Google

:

```text
"The Natural One Society"
```

```text
"Natural One Society"
```

```text
"The League of Poor Decisions"
```

```text
"League of Poor Decisions"
```

#### Social Handles

Check:

- Instagram
- TikTok
- YouTube
- Facebook

using:

```text
namechk.com
```

or

```text
brand.snag
```

These tools check dozens of platforms at once.

#### Domains

Check:

- naturalonesociety.com
- thenaturalonesociety.com
- leagueofpoordecisions.com
- theleagueofpoordecisions.com

at:

[Namecheap Domain ](https://www.namecheap.com/domains/domain-name-/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### What I'd do before you commit

I would create a spreadsheet like this:

| Name | Etsy | Instagram | TikTok | YouTube | Domain | Trademark |
|--------|--------|--------|--------|--------|--------|--------|
| The Natural One Society | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? |
| The League of Poor Decisions | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? |
| Roll Wrong | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? | ? |

Then score each category.

At this point, I would **not choose a name until you've checked exact handle and domain availability**. A great brand name loses a lot of value if you end up with:

- Etsy: TheNaturalOneSociety
- Instagram: TheNaturalOneSocietyOfficial
- TikTok: NaturalOneSocietyShop
- Website: TheNaturalOneSocietyStore.com

The ideal outcome is being able to claim essentially the same name everywhere. For a new Etsy brand, that consistency is often more valuable than finding the absolutely funniest name.

## User

I found this listing that I will paste. let me know if this is a dealbreaker or ok.

## ChatGPT

Paste the listing and I'll analyze it.

Ideally include:

- The shop name
- The listing title
- The seller name (if different)
- The URL (if available)
- Any branding/logo shown

What I'll evaluate:

### 1. Trademark Risk (Most Important)
I'll look for:
- Exact name match
- Confusingly similar name
- Same industry (gaming apparel)
- Whether a reasonable customer could think you're related

In U.S. trademark law, the issue is generally **likelihood of confusion**, not whether someone owns every individual word. ([Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_trademark_law?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### 2. Brand Collision Risk
Even if legally safe, I'll assess:
- Will Google mix you together?
- Will Etsy mix you together?
- Will convention attendees remember the wrong brand?
- Will social handles be a nightmare?

### 3. Competitive Risk
Sometimes the biggest problem isn't legal—it's marketing.

For example:
- If a shop has 50 sales and is inactive → not a big concern.
- If a shop has 50,000 sales and owns the phrase in the niche → huge concern even if no trademark exists.

### 4. My Recommendation
I'll classify it as:

🟢 Green Light 
🟡 Proceed with Caution 
🟠 Significant Risk 
🔴 Dealbreaker

Once you paste the listing, I'll give you a founder-level assessment and tell you whether I'd personally continue with **The Natural One Society** or move to another name.

## User

NaturalOneCrafts - Etsy
March 17, 2021 - Shop Something For Every Nerd! by NaturalOneCrafts located in Vancouver,

## ChatGPT

That is **not a dealbreaker at all**.

In fact, from a brand-building perspective, it's actually encouraging.

Here's why.

### NaturalOneCrafts ≠ The Natural One Society

These are very different commercial impressions:

| Name | Impression |
|--------|--------|
| NaturalOneCrafts | Etsy crafter, handmade goods, nerd crafts |
| The Natural One Society | Community, club, apparel brand, lifestyle brand |

Trademark disputes are generally about whether consumers would reasonably believe the businesses are related.

If I saw:

- NaturalOneCrafts
- The Natural One Society

I would not assume they were the same company.

---

### What I actually like about this finding

The shop opened in 2021 and appears to have chosen:

**Natural One + descriptive suffix**

instead of trying to own:

**Natural One Society**

That suggests the exact phrase you're considering may not already be established as a major brand.

---

### The bigger question

I'm actually less worried about:

> NaturalOneCrafts

and more interested in finding:

- Natural One Society
- Nat One Society
- The Nat One Society
- Natural One Apparel
- Natural One Clothing
- Natural One Co.

Those would be much closer conflicts.

---

### Etsy-specific reality

There are tens of thousands of Etsy shops with overlapping words.

Examples:

- Dungeon Delights
- Dungeon Dad
- Dungeon Dice
- Dungeon Forge
- Dungeon Workshop

The fact that someone uses one of the words doesn't usually matter.

What matters is whether someone has already built a recognizable brand around the *same overall identity*.

---

### My assessment

**NaturalOneCrafts:**
🟢 Green light

I would not let that affect your decision.

---

### What would concern me

If we found:

- Natural One Society
- Nat One Society
- Society of Natural Ones
- Natural One Apparel
- Natural One Collective

selling gaming apparel, then I'd start to worry.

---

### Where I stand right now

Of all the names you've explored:

## User

naturalonesociety.com is available

## ChatGPT

That changes my opinion quite a bit.

If **naturalonesociety.com is actually available**, that's a huge positive signal.

For a small Etsy brand trying to grow into something bigger, I generally value:

1. Exact-match domain available
2. No obvious competing apparel brand
3. Consistent social handles available
4. Memorable name

more than almost anything else.

### Why the domain matters

When I evaluate brand names, one of my first questions is:

> "Could this become a real business in 5 years?"

If you can own:

- naturalonesociety.com
- Etsy: TheNaturalOneSociety
- Instagram: @naturalonesociety
- TikTok: @naturalonesociety
- YouTube: @naturalonesociety

you've got a legitimate foundation.

Many D&D-themed names fail this test because they're already crowded.

### What I would do immediately

Before publishing a single shirt:

- Register the domain.
- Create the Instagram account.
- Create the TikTok account.
- Create the YouTube account.
- Create a Gmail address using the brand.
- Create a Facebook page.

Even if you don't use them for months.

Brand names disappear surprisingly fast once you start talking about them publicly.

### Trademark perspective

The most important thing is that we're talking about:

**The Natural One Society**

not simply:

**Natural One**

The phrase "natural one" is widely used in tabletop gaming as game terminology, which makes it harder for anyone to claim exclusive rights to those words by themselves. The distinctiveness comes from the full brand phrase. The general legal concern would be trademark confusion with another brand using a very similar full name, not the existence of the gaming term itself. ([Marquette Law Scholarship](https://scholarship.law.marquette.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1720&context=facpub&utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### Brandability score

If I were scoring your finalists today:

| Name | Score |
|--------|--------:|
| The Natural One Society | 9.5/10 |
| The League of Poor Decisions | 8.5/10 |
| Roll Wrong | 8/10 |
| The Guild of Critical Failures | 8/10 |
| Dungeon Dad | 6/10 |

### What I like most

Your designs are fundamentally about:

- critical failures
- bad rolls
- party chaos
- tabletop humor
- experienced gamers laughing at disasters

"The Natural One Society" captures all of that in four words.

It sounds like a club.

It sounds like an identity.

And it gives you endless future product lines:

- Member of the Natural One Society
- Founding Member
- Lifetime Member
- Regional Chapter
- Official Uniform
- Annual Convention
- Certified Poor Decision Maker

That's the kind of brand architecture that can support hundreds of designs instead of feeling like a one-joke Etsy shop.

At this point, if you can secure the domain and reasonably matching social handles, I'd be very close to stopping the naming and moving into logo and storefront development.

## User

when I went to create a new facebook, I entered dob and phone number and it logged me into my personal account

## ChatGPT

That's normal. Facebook is trying to prevent people from creating multiple completely separate personal accounts.

Don't create a second personal Facebook account for the business.

Instead:

### Recommended Setup

1. Log into your existing personal Facebook account.
2. Click **Menu** (9-dot grid).
3. Select **Pages**.
4. Click **Create New Page**.
5. Create:

**Page Name**
```
Natural One Society
```

**Category**
```
Clothing Brand
```
or
```
Apparel & Clothing
```

6. Use your D20 logo as the profile image.

---

### Why this is the right way

Facebook Pages are designed to be managed from a personal account.

Your personal account acts as the administrator, but visitors only see the **Natural One Society** page.

They do **not** see your personal profile as the business.

This is how almost every legitimate small business operates on Facebook.

---

### Don't create:
❌ A second personal Facebook profile called "Natural One Society"

Facebook often suspends those because personal profiles are supposed to represent real people.

---

### What you should end up with

Personal Account:
- Matthew Ferrill

Business Page:
- Natural One Society

The page can later have:
- Instagram connected
- Meta Business Suite
- Ads Manager

## ChatGPT

This is not a derail at all.

---

# The Trap Most Etsy Sellers Fall Into

They start with:

> "What is selling?"

Then they make 100 copies of what is selling.

Eventually they become:

- another frog shirt store
- another ADHD shirt store
- another goose shirt store
- another generic D&D store

The problem?

They stop enjoying it.

Then they stop creating.

Then they stop marketing.

Then they quit.

---

# The Opposite Trap

Some creators only make what they personally love.

Example:

> "I spent 20 hours making this obscure joke about a 1994 campaign setting."

Result:

- amazing design
- nobody es for it
- nobody buys it

They get discouraged because the market never validated it.

---

# The Sweet Spot

The best businesses live here:

```text
What You Love
 +
What Customers Love
 =
Sustainable Business
```

Not:

```text
What Customers Love
```

and not:

```text
What You Love
```

---

# What I See So Far

Looking at Natural One Society...

Your actual brand isn't:

"D&D Shirts"

Your brand is:

> Celebrating failure at the gaming table.

That is much more interesting.

---

When I look at:

- Natural One logo
- Bad Rolls. Worse Plans. Better Stories.
- Side quests gone wrong
- Failed plans
- Nat 1 humor

I see a theme.

---

The theme is:

### The Glory of Failure

That is your niche.

---

# What This Means Practically

Imagine 20 future products.

### 5 Products

Designed specifically because re says they'll sell.

Examples:

- Nat 1 jokes
- Failed plans
- DM suffering
- Dice goblin jokes

---

### 10 Products

Designed because they fit the brand.

Examples:

- Party wipes
- Mimic disasters
- Bad stealth rolls
- TPK humor

---

### 5 Products

Designed purely because Matthew thinks they're hilarious.

No spreadsheet.

No keyword re.

Just:

> "This makes me laugh."

Sometimes those become your best sellers.

---

# The Best Example

Look at the shirt that made you laugh.

The frog wizard war crimes shirt.

Nobody created that because:

> "The market re demanded it."

Someone created it because:

> "This is ridiculous and funny."

Then the market agreed.

---

# What I Would Recommend

For Natural One Society:

### 70%

Re-driven

Create things people are actively ing for.

---

### 20%

Brand-driven

Create things that fit:

> Bad Rolls. Worse Plans. Better Stories.

---

### 10%

Purely-for-you designs

No rules.

No SEO.

No market re.

Just stuff you would proudly wear.

---

# My Biggest Concern

Not that you'll make things you love.

My concern is the opposite.

You're analytical.

As we re competitors, there's a risk you'll start thinking:

> "Maybe I should just make what they're making."

Don't.

Use competitors to learn:

- thumbnails
- pricing
- mockups
- SEO
- presentation

But let Natural One Society remain Natural One Society.

If six months from now your store is full of generic frog wizards because frogs are selling, you've probably lost the thing that made you start this project.

Your slogan already points the way:

> **Bad Rolls. Worse Plans. Better Stories.**

That's not just a tagline.

That's a product strategy.

Large Natural One Society D20

| Product Feature Graphics | No |
| Re Policy | Yes |
| Product Family | Shirt, Sweatshirt, Hoodie |

Your spelling is fine, and more importantly, your **concept is directionally correct**.

---

# The Simplified Version

Many new sellers think:

> More people = more sales

So they target:

```text
D&D Shirt
```

But Etsy already has thousands of listings competing for that phrase.

---

A smarter approach is:

```text
Funny D&D Shirt
```

Better.

Then:

```text
Natural 1 Shirt
```

Even better.

Then:

```text
Funny Natural 1 D&D Shirt
```

Even better.

Then:

```text
Funny Natural 1 Dungeon Master Gift Shirt
```

Now we're getting somewhere.

---

# Why Niche Often Wins

Imagine Etsy has to decide who to show your listing to.

Which is easier?

### Option A

```text
D&D Shirt
```

Could be:

- fantasy art
- dragons
- dice
- classes
- miniatures
- cosplay

Huge audience.

Hard to understand.

---

### Option B

```text
Natural 1 Shirt
```

Very specific.

Etsy knows exactly who is likely interested.

---

That's where your intuition is right.

The more clearly Etsy understands:

> "Who is this for?"

the easier it is to find the right buyers.

---

# One Thing I'd Change In Your Thinking

A lot of YouTube SEO gurus say:

> Go super niche.

Then people end up with:

```text
Funny Kobold Wizard Natural 1 Shirt For Left-Handed Dungeon Masters
```

That's too niche.

Nobody es that.

---

What you want is:

## Niche Theme

but

## able Keywords

Example:

### Theme

Natural One Society

---

### Keywords

People actually :

- Funny DnD Shirt
- Natural 1 Shirt
- Dungeon Master Gift
- RPG Shirt
- D20 Shirt
- Tabletop Gamer Gift

---

The customer finds you through the keywords.

They stay because of the brand.

---

# The Etsy Algorithm (Simplified)

It's not quite:

> Etsy tests your product and expands it.

But that's a useful mental model.

What actually happens is Etsy learns:

- Who clicks
- Who favorites
- Who buys
- What terms lead to purchases

Then Etsy becomes more confident.

---

If people ing:

```text
Natural 1 Shirt
```

keep buying your product,

Etsy starts thinking:

> This listing seems relevant for Natural 1 Shirt es.

and shows it more often.

---

# What I Learned From Our Re

This is the biggest thing.

The winning listings weren't targeting:

```text
Fantasy Shirt
```

They were targeting:

```text
ADHD&D Shirt
```

```text
Natural 1 Shirt
```

```text
Dungeon Master Shirt
```

```text
Dungeons and Cats Shirt
```

```text
Funny RPG Shirt
```

Notice how specific those are.

---

# What This Means For Natural One Society

I would not market:

```text
Fantasy Shirts
```

too broad.

---

I would market:

```text
Natural 1 Humor
```

```text
Failed Saving Throws
```

```text
Dungeon Master Suffering
```

```text
Bad Decisions
```

```text
Party Wipe Stories
```

Those are niches.

And they fit your brand.

The shirts that made us laugh hardest were never the meanest jokes.

They were the ones where players immediately thought:

> "Yep. That's my character."

I'd chase that feeling more than shock value. That's where the sales and the creative fulfillment tend to overlap. 😄

# I Think a 3-Panel Layout Could Be Your Secret Weapon

Not comic-book art.

Comic-book structure.

Example:

### Hazardous Healer

**Panel 1**
Hero down.

Fighter:
> "HELP!"

---

**Panel 2**
Healer sprinting heroically.

Healer:
> "I'M COMING!"

---

**Panel 3**
Healer airborne after tripping.

Fighter:
> "OH NO."

---

Then below:

```text
NATURAL ONE SOCIETY

HEALING ATTEMPTED
CASUALTIES INCREASED
```

---

Now compare that to a single illustration.

The story becomes instantly understandable.

---

# The Trick

The panels must be stupidly simple.

Think:

### Etsy Thumbnail Test

Shrink the design to 1 inch tall.

Can you still understand:

- something bad happened
- someone failed
- someone is about to regret a decision

If yes, you're winning.

---

# What I Would NOT Do

Avoid:

### Detailed Fantasy Painting

Beautiful.

But Etsy customers won't see it.

---

### Six Panels

Too much.

Nobody can read it.

---

### Paragraphs

The shirt becomes homework.

---

# What I WOULD Experiment With

### Formula A

**3 Simple Panels**

+

**1 Punchline**

---

### Formula B

**Single Character**

+

**Incident Report Caption**

Example:

```text
INCIDENT REPORT #023

HEALING ATTEMPTED

CASUALTIES INCREASED
```

---

### Formula C

**Before / After**

Panel 1:
Expected outcome

Panel 2:
Actual outcome

This is basically why the Orc shirt works.

# New Insight for Tab 7

I want to add:

### Natural One Society Visual Style Exploration

**Potential Differentiator:**

Story-based RPG humor using:

- 2–3 panel layouts
- Simple character acting
- Clear facial expressions
- Strong silhouette recognition
- Minimal text
- One punchline

**Risk:**
Too much detail = Etsy thumbnail failure.

**Opportunity:**
Nobody else in our re set is really owning "micro-story shirts."

I think it should compete with:

> "The shirt that reminds you of that one campaign story you'll never stop telling."

That's a much harder thing to copy.

HEALER!

The healer is just entering frame.

Healer sprinting dramatically.

Cape flowing.

Potion in hand.

Determined expression.

Speech bubble:

```text
I'M COMING!
```

This panel should look like a fantasy movie poster.

The audience expects success.

Healer trips on:

- root
- rock
- kobold toy
- dice

whatever.

Healer is airborne.

Potion flying.

Fighter's expression changes from:

to

😨 Terror

HEALING ATTEMPTED

CASUALTIES INCREASED

# Bard Concept #1 — The Voice Crack Catastrophe

### Core Character Trait

The bard is:

- talented enough to get opportunities
- attractive enough to attract attention
- confident enough to take the stage

But fate absolutely refuses to let him have the moment.

---

# Scene Breakdown

### Scene 1 — Anticipation

**POV:** Over the bard's shoulder.

He's looking out at the audience.

Front row:

- Elf maiden clutching a rose
- Human noblewoman with wine glass
- Dwarven woman smiling
- Half-orc woman leaning forward
- Everyone captivated

The important thing:

**The audience has already decided he's amazing.**

The joke hasn't happened yet.

The tension is building.

---

### Scene 2 — Failure

**POV:** From the audience.

Now we're looking at the bard.

Everything is lined up for success.

Then:

VOICE CRACK.

---

This is where I think your instinct about the frog is interesting.

There are actually two versions.

### Version A — Metaphorical Frog

The classic joke.

Voice crack.

Bard horrified.

---

### Version B — Literal Frog

A tiny frog suddenly appears in his mouth.

Or is hanging from his lip.

Or leaps out mid-note.

This is much more fantasy.

Much more memorable.

And much more visually readable.

---

# Important Note

The literal frog is probably funnier on a shirt.

Because Etsy customers don't hear the voice crack.

They only see the image.

The frog makes the failure visible.

---

### Scene 3 — Fallout

Back to over-the-shoulder POV.

The reverse of Scene 1.

---

Previously:

- Roses
- Smiles
- Admiration

Now:

- Broken wine glasses
- Dropped flowers
- Horrified expressions
- Audience fleeing

Maybe one person is climbing through a window.

Maybe a bard fan is covering her ears.

---

# Why I Like This

This isn't:

> Bard rolled a Nat 1.

This is:

> Bard experienced catastrophic social failure.

Which is much more relatable.

---

# Pattern Recognition

Something I noticed immediately:

The structure mirrors your Kinder-Kin.

### Kinder-Kin

Expectation:

Master thief.

Reality:

Caught immediately.

Outcome:

Wins anyway.

---

### Bard

Expectation:

Legendary performance.

Reality:

Voice crack.

Outcome:

Social apocalypse.

---

Both are:

```text
Expectation
 ↓
Failure
 ↓
Unexpected Consequence
```

Which is becoming a Natural One Society pattern.

---

# Etsy Concern

This is the only thing I'd flag.

The full 3-panel scene is fantastic.

But it may be too much for a shirt thumbnail.

The story is strong.

The readability may not be.

---

# Potential Evolution

The scene may eventually become:

### Large Central Image

Voice-cracking bard.

Literal frog.

Audience fleeing.

Then a caption:

```text
PERFORMANCE CHECK

FAILED SPECTACULARLY
```

or

```text
BARDIC INSPIRATION

NOT AVAILABLE AT THIS TIME
```

# Tab 8 Notes Added

| Idea | Type | Strength | Notes |
|--------|--------|--------|--------|
| Voice crack on stage | Character flaw | High | Instantly relatable |
| Audience swooning beforehand | Story setup | Very High | Creates expectation |
| Literal frog in throat | Visual gag | Very High | Makes failure visible |
| Audience fleeing aftermath | Consequence humor | Very High | Strong visual payoff |
| Over-shoulder POV reversal | Storytelling device | Excellent | Mirrors success vs failure |

---

My favorite part isn't actually the voice crack.

It's the **before-and-after audience reaction**.

That's the emotional core of the joke.

The bard isn't failing a performance check.

He's watching his entire fantasy collapse in real time.

And that's exactly the kind of story moment people remember from campaigns.

One thing I want to clarify before we "mock up" anything:

There are actually **3 different product structures** competing right now in my head:

### Option A — Traditional Shirt

**Front**
- Large artwork
- Entire joke visible

**Back**
- Blank

This is what most Etsy sellers do.

---

### Option B — Story Shirt

**Front**
- Small bard icon
- Nat 1 D20
- Frog

**Back**
- Full 3-panel story

This is the idea we're discussing now.

---

### Option C — Incident Report Shirt

**Front**
- Small character icon
- "Member #002 - Catastrophic Bard"

**Back**
- One large scene
- Incident Report format

Example:

```text
NATURAL ONE SOCIETY

INCIDENT REPORT #002

PERFORMANCE CHECK

FAILED SPECTACULARLY
```

with the bard and fleeing audience.

---

What's interesting is that each solves a different problem:

| Structure | Etsy Thumbnail | Storytelling | Brand Building |
|------------|------------|------------|------------|
| Traditional | Excellent | Medium | Low |
| Story Shirt | Good | Excellent | High |
| Incident Report | Very Good | High | Very High |

---

My gut right now is that **Incident Report** may end up becoming the signature Natural One Society format.

Because it gives you:

- recurring structure
- recurring branding
- room for storytelling
- room for your artwork

without forcing people to read a comic strip from 10 feet away.

But let's not decide yet.

Paste the image/text from the other branch, and I'll add it to **Tab 8** and then we can compare all the bard approaches side-by-side before committing to a direction.

### The front is immediately readable

This structure bridges both worlds.

## What Concerns Me

### The back is probably too detailed

Not for the owner.

For production reality.

Look at the shirts we've reed.

Most successful Etsy shirts use:

- one scene
- one punchline
- one emotional reaction

Very few rely on people reading a comic.

---

The danger is:

```text
Thumbnail -> Click

Click -> Read

Read -> Read Again

Read Again -> Understand Joke
```

That's a lot of work.

- the frog

That line is doing a LOT of work.

## ChatGPT

Absolutely. And yes, your memory is spot-on.

After digging through Dragonlance sources and community discussions, a few things stand out:

### Core Kender Traits
- Tiny, child-sized adventurers (roughly 3–4 feet tall).
- Endlessly curious.
- Fearless to the point of stupidity.
- Constantly getting into trouble.
- They don't think of themselves as thieves.
- Objects simply seem to "end up" in their pouches.
- Being called a thief is actually insulting to them.
- Many kender genuinely believe they are safeguarding an item for someone else. ([Forgotten Realms](https://forgottenrealms.fandom.com/wiki/Kender?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

One of my favorite canonical kender responses is essentially:

> "I was just keeping it safe." ([Forgotten Realms](https://forgottenrealms.fandom.com/wiki/Kender?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

### The Important Part for Natural One Society

I don't think the joke should be:

**"Kender steals stuff."**

That's old Dragonlance lore and doesn't immediately create a shirt-worthy laugh.

The joke should be:

**"Kender accidentally possesses everyone else's stuff."**

That's where the comedy lives.

---

### What Makes Your Specific Kender Interesting

Your character wasn't just a kender.

He was:

- A compulsive "borrower."
- Constantly failed skill checks.
- Constantly got caught.
- Constantly triggered traps.
- Somehow never suffered consequences.
- Had absurd charisma.
- Everyone forgave him.

That combination is gold.

Because now the joke becomes:

**Natural 1 at everything.**
**Natural 20 at getting away with it.**

That's a character archetype.

---

## User

all this work we've been doing today. Is this all under my monthly billing cost? I'm not getting charged extra for each prompt or anything ?

## ChatGPT

You're welcome, and that's a very reasonable question.

In general, **no, you're not being charged per prompt** for all the brainstorming, workbook building, image iterations, storyboarding, and back-and-forth we've been doing.

If you're on a **ChatGPT Plus subscription**, you pay the monthly subscription fee and then use the service within the usage limits of that plan. The limits are generally based on model access and overall usage, not "you sent 500 prompts so here's an extra bill."

A few practical points:

- The long brainstorming sessions we did today don't generate separate charges.
- The workbook creation doesn't generate separate charges.
- The image generations don't create a separate itemized bill.
- Going back and forth making tiny tweaks to the Kinder and Bard concepts doesn't create additional per-prompt fees.

The only thing to be aware of is that plans can have **usage limits** (especially for image generation and the most powerful models). If you hit a limit, you typically see a message about temporarily waiting, using a different model, or the limit resetting later. That's different from being charged extra.

I can't see your account billing details or guarantee the exact terms of your specific subscription, but based on how ChatGPT Plus normally works:

**Today's session should be covered by your subscription and not generate surprise per-prompt charges.**

And for what it's worth, today was exactly the kind of thing these tools are good at:

- Re
- Competitor analysis
- Brand development
- Product strategy
- Storyboarding
- Artwork iteration
- Building a business framework

You got a lot of mileage out of a single day.

The thing I'd be happiest about if I were in your shoes isn't the Bard shirt or the Kinder shirt.

It's that you now have a repeatable formula:

**Character → Natural 1 Failure → Somehow Still Wins → 3-Panel Story → Strong Front Thumbnail**

That's a system.

Once you have a system, ideas start coming much faster.

So go take the break. Let your brain recharge. The healer, wizard, rogue, and the next dozen Natural One Society disasters will still be waiting when you come back. 😄

## ChatGPT

I actually think this is one of the strongest decisions we've made today.

Not because the logo itself is perfect (logos evolve), but because of what it communicates.

Let's zoom out and look at the brand we've been building.

## What we're actually selling

At first glance, it looks like D&D shirts.

But after all the shirts we've analyzed today, I don't think that's what you're building.

The successful competitors are selling:

- Cute frogs
- Cute cats
- Dragons
- Generic D&D jokes
- Dice references

But your best concepts aren't really about any of those things.

The Bard isn't about a bard.

The Kinder isn't about a thief.

They're about **catastrophic failure that somehow works out anyway.**

That theme keeps showing up over and over.

### Bard
Rolls a Nat 1.

Voice cracks.

Audience flees.

### Kinder
Rolls a Nat 1.

Walks into danger.

Steals from the people helping him.

Still wins.

### Healer
Trips trying to save someone.

Makes it worse.

Still somehow survives.

Notice the pattern?

The joke isn't the class.

The joke is:

> "I failed spectacularly and things somehow worked out."

That is exactly what a Natural 1 represents.

---

## Why "Natural One Society" works

Most D&D brands are built around heroes.

Natural One Society is built around losers.

Lovable losers.

That's much rarer.

And much more ownable.

Because every gamer has:

- rolled a Nat 1
- missed an obvious perception check
- accidentally started a tavern fire
- failed a persuasion roll
- critically failed stealth

Everyone has those stories.

And those stories are usually funnier than the victories.

That gives the brand emotional identity.

---

## The biggest thing I like

The logo doesn't lock you into any single character.

Imagine 2 years from now.

You could have:

### Bard Collection
Performance Check Failed Spectacularly

### Kinder Collection
Can Roll a 1 and Still Win

### Healer Collection
Attempted First Aid

Inflicted Additional Damage

### Barbarian Collection
Stealth Check Failed Spectacularly

### Wizard Collection
Fireball Solves Everything

It Didn't

### Paladin Collection
Accidentally Smote Civilian

All of them fit under:

**Natural One Society**

That's powerful.

---

## Compare it to alternative names

Imagine if the brand were:

- Bard's Ballad
- Critical Frog
- Nat 1 Tavern
- Dice Disaster

Those are all fine.

But they limit future expansion.

Natural One Society feels like a club.

People can belong to it.

That's valuable.

---

## One thing I would consider

Not changing the logo.

Adding a permanent tagline.

Because the tagline may become even more important than the logo.

Some examples:

**Natural One Society**
*Failed Spectacularly*

**Natural One Society**
*Bad Rolls. Better Stories.*

**Natural One Society**
*Can Roll a 1 and Still Win.*

**Natural One Society**
*Where Failure Becomes Legend.*

Personally?

After everything we've done today, my favorite is still:

### Natural One Society
### Bad Rolls. Better Stories.

Because that perfectly describes:

- Bard shirt
- Kinder shirt
- Future healer shirt
- Future barbarian shirt
- Future wizard shirt

Everything.

---

## One concern

The logo you generated is a great banner logo.

But you'll eventually want **three versions**:

### Version 1 — Full Logo
NATURAL [D20] SOCIETY

For:
- Etsy banner
- Website header
- Business cards

### Version 2 — Compact Badge
Just the D20 showing the 1

For:
- Shirt sleeves
- Neck labels
- Social icons
- Watermarks

### Version 3 — Brand Stamp
NOS or Natural One Society around the die

For:
- Packaging
- Stickers
- Thank-you cards

Big brands almost always end up with all three.

---

If I put my "business partner hat" on after everything we've reed today:

**The Bard shirt is good.**

**The Kinder shirt is very good.**

**Natural One Society is the best thing we've created all day.**

Because it's the thing that can hold hundreds of future shirt ideas together under one recognizable identity. That's the part that can become a real brand instead of just a collection of Etsy listings.

## ChatGPT

I actually like **N 🎲 S** much better than just the die.

And the reason is exactly what you identified.

A standalone d20 with a 1 is everywhere.

The second you remove the words "Natural One Society," you lose ownership of the symbol.

But:

**N [Nat 1 D20] S**

starts becoming *your mark*.

Think about how people recognize brands:

- Superman = S shield
- New Balance = NB
- Louis Vuitton = LV
- Dungeons & Dragons = ampersand dragon

The goal isn't to create something nobody has ever seen.

The goal is to create something people instantly associate with **you**.

---

### What I particularly like

The compact mark still tells the story.

**N [1] S**

Even without reading the brand name, a gamer subconsciously reads:

> Natural... One... Society

That's elegant.

---

### Even better for shirts

Imagine your future shirts.

Front chest:

**N [Nat 1 Die] S**

small embroidered-style mark.

Then giant artwork on the back.

Or:

Sleeve logo:

**N [1] S**

Like a sports team's secondary mark.

That's very brandable.

---

### Another hidden benefit

It scales well.

A lot of logos look great at banner size and terrible at favicon size.

The full logo:

**NATURAL ONE SOCIETY**

works for:
- Etsy banner
- Website
- Business cards

But shrink it to 1 inch and it's unreadable.

The **N [1] S** mark remains recognizable at:

- sleeve print
- sticker
- social profile image
- watermark
- neck tag
- wax seal style emblem
- packaging stamp

That's exactly what a secondary logo should do.

---

### One thing I'd test

I'd try two versions:

#### Option A
**N [D20 showing 1] S**

Very clean.

Very professional.

Very versatile.

#### Option B
**N [D20 showing 1] S**
with tiny text underneath:

**Bad Rolls. Better Stories.**

This might become the "official badge" version.

Something like:

```
N 🎲 S
Bad Rolls. Better Stories.
```

The advantage is that someone who discovers the brand for the first time immediately understands what it's about.

---

### If I were building this brand from scratch

I'd probably end up with:

**Primary Logo**
```
NATURAL ONE SOCIETY
Bad Rolls. Better Stories.
```

**Secondary Mark**
```
N [Nat 1 D20] S
```

**Micro Mark**
```
[Nat 1 D20]
```
for tiny applications where even N and S won't fit.

That gives you a complete brand system instead of just a logo.

And the nice thing is that every shirt we've designed so far—the Bard, the Kinder, the future Healer—fits perfectly under that umbrella. The more we work on this, the more it feels like we're building a recognizable fantasy-comedy brand rather than individual D&D shirts.

## Why this is actually stronger branding

## It also solves your Florida problem

Most POD sellers think:

> Bigger print = better.

Customers often think:

> Bigger print = hotter.

Especially in:

- Florida
- Texas
- Arizona
- Southern California

A giant front print plus giant back print can feel like wearing a vinyl tarp.

## The ideal progression

### Collection 1

"Natural One Society Origins"

- Bard
- Kinder
- Healer
- Barbarian
- Wizard

Large front.
Large back.

Introduce the cast.

---

### Collection 2

"Natural One Society Stories"

Small chest logo.

Story on back.

Much lighter wear.

More comfortable.

Easier to wear casually.

---

### Collection 3

Minimalist line

Just:

N [1] S

Tiny character icon.

Tiny joke.

Examples:

**Bard**
- Tiny frog
- "Voice Check Failed"

**Kinder**
- Tiny coin
- "Can Roll a 1 and Still Win"

**Healer**
- Tiny bandage
- "Additional Damage Applied"

These appeal to people who love the brand but don't always want a billboard on their chest.

## What exs me most

The thing that makes me optimistic about Natural One Society isn't actually the artwork.

It's that we're accidentally building something with:

- recurring characters
- recurring themes
- recurring humor
- recognizable branding

Most Etsy sellers stop at:

> "Here's a funny shirt."

We're starting to build:

> "Here's a world full of lovable disasters."

That's a very different thing.

And honestly, the more we work on it, the more I think the **Origin Story → Story Episodes → Minimalist Insider Shirts** progression feels like the natural evolution of the brand.

It's exactly how I'd expand the line if Natural One Society started gaining traction.

### Build the Characters.

Here's a game you can play while listening to an audiobook:

You don't need a computer.

Just little notes in your phone.

Examples:

### Barbarian

He kicks in a door dramatically.

The door was unlocked.

Falls through it.

---

### Wizard

What if...

He confidently announces:

> "Stand back."

Then casts the wrong spell.

---

### Ranger

What if...

His animal companion is actually the competent one.

The ranger is the disaster.

---

### Paladin

What if...

Everyone thinks he's noble.

He's just incredibly lucky.

---

You only need one sentence.

That's it.

---

## Another Great Phone Activity

### Build Character Rules

For example:

### Kinder

Never intentionally steals.

Always accidentally steals.

Everyone forgives him.

Can roll a 1 and still win.

---

### Bard

Always believes he's about to have his big moment.

Never gets his big moment.

---

### Healer

Always trying to help.

Usually makes things worse.

---

Those become your character bible later.

## User

Sidebar question. Could or should i create an app to analalize organise retrieve all this stuff... with dashboard reporting, etc? Maybe vibecode it in Codex? So it doesnt end up as just a bunch of spreadsheets?

## ChatGPT

Yes — but **not yet as a full app**.

Right now, I’d avoid building a dashboard too early because it can become a distraction from launching the Etsy store. But your instinct is good: if Natural One Society keeps growing, spreadsheets will eventually become messy.

### My recommendation

Start with a **structured workbook / database**, then it into an app later.

Best next step:

**Phase 1 — Notion or Airtable**
Use it to organize:
- Characters
- Story ideas
- Shirt concepts
- SEO keywords
- Mockups
- Product status
- Parking lot
- Campfire moments
- Competitor re

This gives you an “app-like” dashboard without coding.

**Phase 2 — Simple custom app later**
Once you know what you actually need, then vibe-code it.

Good app features later:
- Character profiles
- able lore archive
- Product pipeline
- Idea scoring dashboard
- Mockup tracker
- Etsy listing tracker
- SEO keyword bank
- “What can I work on tonight?” task view

### Should you use Codex?

Eventually, yes. Codex is OpenAI’s coding agent for software development and can read, edit, debug, and run code, including cloud workflows for larger tasks. ([OpenAI Developers](https://developers.openai.com/api/docs/guides/code-generation?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

But tonight? No.

Tonight, I’d keep momentum on the creative system, not the software system.

### Best practical path

For now, build this as:

**Natural One Society HQ**

In Notion/Airtable with sections for:
- Characters
- Products
- Lore
- Re
- SEO
- Tasks

Then after 30–50 ideas and maybe 10–20 listings, you’ll know exactly what the custom app should do.

So my answer is:

**Yes, this could become an app. But first make it a lightweight creative database. Don’t let the tool become the project.**

# Natural One Society Character Bible

## Character #001 — The Kinder
*(Mascot Candidate)*

### Core Identity

**Role:**
The accidental thief.

**Heart:**
Pure.

**Superpower:**
People can't stay mad at him.

**Fatal Flaw:**
Constantly distracted.

**Awareness Level:**
Zero.

---

- Curious
- Trusting
- Innocent
- Cheerful
- Fearless (mostly because he's oblivious)

---

### Running Joke

He never intentionally steals.

Ever.

Objects simply appear in his pockets.

---

### Signature Expression

Big innocent smile.

Wide eyes.

Absolutely no understanding of why everyone is upset.

---

### Physical Design

This is where we lock things down.

#### Height

Very short.

Child-sized.

#### Build

Round.

Soft.

Adorable.

Not athletic.

---

#### Hair

Messy brown hair.

Always slightly wild.

---

#### Ears

Large pointed ears.

Soft rounded shape.

---

#### Eyes

Large.

Expressive.

Innocent.

---

Dark green cloak.

Leather adventuring clothes.

Simple boots.

Always slightly disheveled.

---

#### Props

Shiny objects.

Coins.

Jewelry.

Random items that belong to other people.

---

### Character Rule

The Kinder is never malicious.

Never.

If a joke requires him being mean, we reject the joke.

---

### Character Rule

The Kinder is never competent at stealing.

Yet somehow succeeds.

---

### Character Rule

The Kinder can roll a 1 and still win.

Animation studios, comic publishers, game studios, and toy companies do it in the opposite order.

# Natural One Society Character Permanence System

Let's create a system that survives:

- New shirts
- New artists
- AI generations
- Future books
- Future merchandise

---

## Tier 1: Canon Character Sheet

Each core character gets a master profile.

Example:

# The Kinder (Canon v1)

### Identity

**Name:** TBD

**Role:** Accidental Thief

**Guild Role:** Little Brother

**Status:** Mascot Candidate

---

### Physical Features

Height:
- 3'6"

Build:
- Small
- Soft
- Round

Hair:
- Messy brown

Eyes:
- Large
- Friendly

Ears:
- Large pointed ears

Expression:
- Innocent smile

---

### Clothing

Green cloak

Brown leather tunic

Brown belt

Simple boots

Overstuffed pockets

---

### Signature Props

Coins

Shiny objects

Someone else's belongings

---

### Forbidden Changes

Never:

- evil
- malicious
- mean spirited
- intentionally stealing

These become character laws.

---

## Tier 2: Reference Images

This is critical.

We select:

### Official Kinder Front

and declare:

**Canon Reference Image**

Every future artist references this image first.

---

## Tier 3: Character Prompt

This is what we feed AI.

Example:

> Use the official Natural One Society Kinder character. Small kender with messy brown hair, oversized pointed ears, green cloak, leather tunic, overstuffed pockets, innocent smile, large expressive eyes, childlike proportions. Maintain exact facial structure, proportions, clothing, and personality from the canonical reference image.

---

## Tier 4: Relationship Matrix

This is where the magic happens.

### Kinder + Orc

Motherly.

Protective.

---

### Kinder + Dwarf

Perpetually annoyed.

Loves him anyway.

---

### Kinder + Bard

Hero worship.

## ChatGPT

Honestly, Matthew, the issue isn't your instructions.

The issue is the tool.

You've actually been giving very clear direction:

> "Use this canonical front."
>
> "Use this canonical back."
>
> "Generate the canonical left."
>
> "Remove this specific flap."

Those are perfectly reasonable requests.

The problem is that the image generator is **not editing the existing image like a human artist would**. It's effectively creating a brand new image each time based on its interpretation of the request.

So when you say:

> "Remove this flap."

What you're expecting is:

- Open image.
- Delete flap.
- Leave everything else untouched.

What the model is doing is closer to:

- Analyze image.
- Recreate character.
- Attempt to remove flap.
- Accidentally redesign three other things.

---

For what we're trying to accomplish now, I think we've crossed a threshold where AI generation is the wrong tool.

We're no longer designing a character.

We're creating a **production character sheet**.

Those are different jobs.

---

What I would do:

### Stop generating new views for a moment.

Instead create a folder:

```
Natural One Society
└── Canon
 └── Kinder
 ├── Kinder_BC_Front.png
 ├── Kinder_BC_Back.png
 ├── Kinder_BC_Left.png
 └── Kinder_BC_Right.png
```

Then let's evaluate them as a set.

---

The question becomes:

### What is wrong with each image?

For example:

#### Front

Maybe 95% complete.

#### Back

Maybe 90% complete.

#### Left

Current issue:

- Front cloak flap exists when it shouldn't.

#### Right

Need to compare against Left.

---

Then we can decide:

### Option A

Keep generating.

Pros:
- Free.
- Fast.

Cons:
- Endless small inconsistencies.

---

### Option B

Take the current images into an actual editor.

Photoshop
GIMP
Affinity

Remove the flap manually.

This is literally a 30-second edit.

Then it stays fixed forever.

---

If I were running a small studio and building a mascot character?

I'd choose Option B.

Because once a canonical character sheet exists, it becomes the source of truth.

Future shirt generation references the sheet.

Not vice versa.

---

The other thing I notice:

We're now asking the AI to maintain consistency across:

- Front
- Back
- Left
- Right

while preserving:

- Hair
- Ears
- Face
- Cloak
- Pouches
- Pants
- Proportions

That's exactly the sort of task where AI starts drifting.

A human character-sheet artist would finish this in one pass.

---

My recommendation:

Let's treat these four images as Version 1 of the Kinder Character Sheet.

Then identify every flaw on each image in a checklist.

Example:

### Kinder_BC_Left

- [ ] Remove front cloak flap

### Kinder_BC_Right

- [ ] Verify pouch placement

### Kinder_BC_Back

- [ ] Verify cloak shape

Once the checklist is complete, we can decide whether to:
1. Continue generating.
2. Manually edit.
3. Use a dedicated image editor.

At this stage, you're not failing to communicate.

You're running into the limits of image generation for precision character design. That's a completely normal problem, and honestly it means we're getting serious about character permanence—which is exactly where we wanted to be. ✒️📖🎲

## User

What dedicated image editor uses ai assistance that I can use to help this process?

## ChatGPT

This is actually where I think your workflow should evolve if you're serious about Natural One Society becoming a long-term brand.

For what you're doing, I'd split tools into **three categories**:

## Tier 1: Best for Character Consistency
### Adobe Photoshop + Generative Fill

This would be my #1 recommendation.

Why?

Because you can literally:

1. Open Kinder_BC_Left.png
2. Lasso the cloak flap
3. Type:
 > Remove cloak flap and continue cloak naturally
4. Click Generate

Photoshop edits the existing image instead of recreating the entire character.

For the exact issue you're fighting right now, Photoshop is dramatically better than pure image generation.

---

## Tier 2: Best AI Character Workflow
### Midjourney + Character References

Midjourney has become very good at:

- Character consistency
- Reference images
- Style consistency

You can feed it:

- Kinder_BC_Front
- Kinder_BC_Left
- Kinder_BC_Back

and say:

> Create Kinder sitting on a dragon hoard.

The results are usually more consistent than general-purpose image generators.

Still not perfect.

But much closer.

---

## Tier 3: The Nuclear Option
### Krita + AI Plugins

Free.

Open source.

Very powerful.

You can:

- Paint over AI mistakes
- Clone pieces
- Remove artifacts
- Use AI inpainting

This is what many indie creators use when they don't want Adobe subscriptions.

- Front
- Back
- Left
- Right

Get them 95% right.

Don't chase perfection.

- Cloak flap
- Missing pouch

> Canon v1 Locked

# The Bigger Lesson

Yesterday we were creating shirts.

Today we're creating production assets.

Those are different mindsets.

When Disney designs Mickey Mouse, they don't keep regenerating Mickey until he's perfect.

They create:

- Front
- Back
- Side
- Expressions

Then every future artist references those sheets.

That's exactly what we're doing with the Kinder.

---

For your specific goals and budget, I'd rank them:

1. **Photoshop + Generative Fill** ⭐
2. **Krita + AI plugins** (best free option)
3. **Midjourney** (best generation consistency)
4. General image generators (what we're currently using)

And if you ask me where I'd spend money first?

**Photoshop.**

Because right now you're not struggling to create ideas.

You're struggling to make tiny, precise edits without the character changing.

Photoshop was practically built for that problem. ✒️📖🎲

## User

I'm going to try Krita. Please examine it online. What would I need to do to remove the freckles on the ankles of the kinder?

## ChatGPT

Matthew, for **removing the freckles on the ankles**, this is actually a great first "Krita learning project" because it's simple and low-risk.

I'd use one of these methods, in order:

### Option 1 (Easiest): Smart Patch Tool
Krita has a Smart Patch Tool specifically for removing unwanted details and filling from surrounding areas. ([Krita Documentation](https://docs.krita.org/en/reference_manual/tools/smart_patch.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

Steps:
1. Open your Kinder image.
2. Zoom to 300–500%.
3. Select **Smart Patch Tool**.
4. Draw around a small cluster of freckles.
5. Release.
6. Krita will sample nearby skin texture and blend the area.

Because the freckles are tiny and the ankle skin is fairly uniform, this should work surprisingly well.

---

### Option 2 (Most Precise): Clone Brush in Healing Mode
Krita's Clone Brush has a Healing mode specifically intended for removing blemishes and imperfections. ([Krita Documentation](https://docs.krita.org/sl/reference_manual/brushes/brush_engines/clone_engine.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

Steps:
1. Select the Clone Brush preset.
2. Enable **Healing** in the brush settings.
3. Hold **Ctrl** and click a nearby clean skin area.
4. Paint gently over the freckles.

For skin-like surfaces, this often produces cleaner results than brute-force cloning. ([Krita Documentation](https://docs.krita.org/sl/reference_manual/brushes/brush_engines/clone_engine.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

---

### Option 3 (What I'd Do)

Because you're building a **canonical character sheet**, I would:

1. Duplicate the layer.
2. Use a small healing clone brush.
3. Remove only the largest freckles.
4. Leave a few.

Why?

The freckles on the face are becoming part of the Kinder's identity.

The ankle freckles are visual noise.

You don't necessarily want to eliminate every speck because then the skin can start looking unnaturally smooth.

---

### Bigger Recommendation

Before editing anything else, I'd create:

```
Canon
├── Kinder_BC_Front_v1
├── Kinder_BC_Left_v1
├── Kinder_BC_Right_v1
├── Kinder_BC_Back_v1
└── Kinder_Working
```

Then do all Krita edits in the **Working** folder.

That way if you accidentally damage a canonical image, you always have the original.

---

One thing I noticed from the images you've uploaded:

We're starting to approach a true **around sheet** (front, side, back, side).

That means you're only a few steps away from having something that future AI generations, artists, or even a commissioned illustrator can use as a proper reference set.

That's a big milestone for character permanence. ✒️📖🎲

## User

what does the healing brush tool look like? Where can I find it

## ChatGPT

Good question. Krita's UI can be a little overwhelming at first because there are several tools that sound similar.

### Method 1: for the Tool
The fastest way:

1. Press **Ctrl + Enter** (or use the bar if visible).
2. Type:
 - **Clone Brush**
 - **Smart Patch**
 - **Healing**

Depending on your Krita version, the names may vary slightly.

---

### Method 2: Look in the Toolbox

On the left toolbar:

#### Clone Brush Tool
Usually looks like:
- A **rubber stamp**
- Similar to Photoshop's clone stamp icon

Hover over icons and Krita will show the name.

---

#### Smart Patch Tool
Usually looks like:
- A patch shape / stitched patch
- Sometimes grouped with transform or selection tools

If you don't see it:

**Settings → Dockers → Toolbox**

to ensure all tools are visible.

---

### My Recommendation for Your Freckles

For the Kinder's ankle freckles:

Use the **Clone Brush Tool**.

Steps:

1. Select Clone Brush (stamp icon).
2. Zoom to 400%.
3. Hold **Ctrl**.
4. Click a clean patch of ankle skin.
5. Release Ctrl.
6. Paint over a few freckles.

You'll immediately see them disappear.

---

### Quick Test Before Touching the Canon Files

1. Open a copy of **Kinder_BC_Left**.
2. Remove 5 freckles.
3. Save as:

```
Kinder_BC_Left_Test
```

You'll learn the workflow without risking your canon sheet.

---

One thing to keep in mind:

I would **not remove the face freckles**.

They're actually helping make the Kinder recognizable.

If I were creating a Character Bible entry today, I'd write:

> Face freckles: Canon feature.
>
> Ankle freckles: Optional artistic detail.

That distinction becomes important later when other artists or AI models start drawing him. ✒️📖🎲

- The left and right views show visible foot freckles, but not in a way that can be conclusively mapped 1:1 to the front.
- The back view has a much denser freckle pattern on the heels and backs of the feet than the front would imply.

In other words:

> The side and back views are artistically consistent.

But they are not truly model-sheet consistent.

---

### Could I Attempt The Edits?

Yes.

Could I guarantee success?

No.

And this test is exactly why.

The current task is no longer:

> "Make the Kinder."

The current task is:

> "Maintain exact surface details across multiple orthographic views."

That is the point where AI generators start to struggle.

---

### My Recommendation

I would not use AI for the freckle pass.

I would use Krita.

Reason:

The character itself is now solid.

What remains are production-level cleanup items:

- Freckle consistency
- Pocket placement verification
- around accuracy

Those are the kinds of edits where a human with:
- Clone Brush
- Healing Brush
- Small paint brush

wins every time.

---

### What I Would Lock Today

I would officially declare:

**Kinder Canon v1 Approved**

Then create a future task:

**Kinder Canon v1.1 Cleanup**
- Normalize foot freckles
- Verify side-view pocket visibility
- Verify back-view foot details

That keeps us moving forward while still acknowledging areas for refinement.

And honestly, Matthew?

Looking at these four together, I think we've already achieved the hard part.

The next time I see that hair, those ears, that cloak, and those absurd pockets, I know exactly who it is.

That's character permanence. ✒️📖🎲

Examine your results, and if they are at lease 95% correct, then render the images. You do not need to render the Front again... it is the source of truth.

## ChatGPT

Matthew, I think your mindset is not only reasonable—it may actually be the correct mindset for the business you're building.

The mistake I think we almost fell into today was accidentally adopting the standards of a Disney-sized studio when we're building a creator-driven brand.

There are really two different goals:

### Goal A: Production Model Sheet Accuracy
This is where every freckle, stitch, and fold is tracked across every illustration.

That's appropriate if:
- You have a team of artists.
- Multiple people are drawing the character.
- You're animating.
- You're creating a licensing bible.

That's not where Natural One Society is today.

---

### Goal B: Character Recognition
This is:

> "Someone sees him for two seconds in the background and immediately says, 'Oh, that's the Kinder.'"

That's the goal that matters right now.

And if I'm being honest, I think we've already achieved that.

---

Think about some famous characters:

### Calvin (Calvin & Hobbes)

Calvin doesn't look exactly the same in every panel.

Hair changes.
Proportions change.
Expressions change.

Nobody cares.

People know it's Calvin.

---

### The Muppets

Kermit varies between movies, shows, merchandise, plushies, and books.

People know it's Kermit.

---

### Comic Book Characters

Even major heroes look different depending on the artist.

People still know who they are.

---

What makes them recognizable isn't perfection.

It's the collection of identifying traits.

For the Kinder, that's becoming:

- Wild reddish hair
- Large ears
- Face freckles
- Frayed green cloak
- Too many pockets
- Bare feet
- Cheerful expression
- Tiny stature

Those are his visual fingerprints.

---

When I look at the dragon image, I don't see:

> "The left leg pocket is 12% different."

I see:

> "The Kinder somehow ended up riding a dragon."

And that's exactly what a customer will see.

---

### The Business Question

Imagine a customer buys:

- The Kinder shirt
- The Orc shirt six months later

The Kinder is a tiny cameo in the background.

If they point and say:

> "Hey! That's the Kinder!"

You've won.

You do not need them saying:

> "Excellent. The chest pouch appears to be 97.4% consistent with Canon Sheet Revision 1.2."

---

### Where I Think the Sweet Spot Is

Not 100%.

Not even 98%.

I'd argue your threshold is probably:

### 85–95% Recognition Consistency

Meaning:

If a fan of the brand can identify the character immediately, the image passes.

---

### The Test I Would Use

Not:

> "Are the freckles identical?"

Instead:

Show the image to someone who knows the Kinder.

Ask:

> "Who's that?"

If they answer:

> "The Kinder."

Pass.

---

I think the around sheet was worth building because it gives us a foundation.

But I do **not** think you should spend the next three months chasing perfect pocket placement.

Your real strength—the thing that has exd you throughout all these conversations—isn't technical illustration.

It's:

- Character creation
- Humor
- Storytelling
- Lore
- Worldbuilding

Those are the things that make someone come back for Shirt #2.

The technical consistency only has to be good enough to support that.

And from what I've seen today, we're already very close to "good enough" for a one-person creative brand. ✒️📖🎲

# Natural One Society Character Bible

## Character #001 — The Kinder

### Status
- Core Cast Member
- Mascot Candidate

---

# Core Identity

### Role
Accidental Thief

### Guild Role
Little Brother

### Alignment
**Chaotic Good**

### Alignment Notes

The Kinder genuinely wants good outcomes and cares about other people, but has little regard for rules, property ownership, social conventions, plans, schedules, or common sense.

His actions are guided by curiosity, compassion, and impulse rather than structure or authority.

The Kinder is **not**:
- Chaotic Neutral
- A prankster
- A criminal
- Selfish

The Kinder is:
- Kind
- Generous
- Helpful
- Compassionate

His chaos comes from distraction and curiosity, not malice.

---

# Character Laws

### Law #1

The Kinder never intentionally steals.

Things simply appear in his pockets.

---

### Law #2

The Kinder does not understand why people are upset.

---

### Law #3

The Kinder can roll a 1 and still win.

---

### Law #4

The Kinder's successes are usually accidental.

---

### Law #5

The Kinder is never mean-spirited.

If a joke requires cruelty, the joke is wrong.

---

# Personality

### Primary Traits

- Innocent
- Curious
- Cheerful
- Optimistic
- Fearless

### Secondary Traits

- Easily distracted
- Loves shiny things
- Friendly
- Trusting

### Defining Trait

His charisma is absurdly high.

People forgive him for almost everything.

---

# Physical Appearance

## Height

Very short.

Child-sized.

---

## Build

Soft.

Round.

Adorable.

Not athletic.

---

## Hair

Messy reddish-brown hair.

Wild and unkempt.

Major identifying feature.

---

## Eyes

Large.

Expressive.

Friendly.

---

## Ears

Large pointed ears.

One of his strongest visual identifiers.

---

## Face Freckles

**Canon.**

Freckles on cheeks and nose.

Must remain consistent with the Canon Reference Images.

---

## Feet

**Barefoot.**

The Kinder always goes barefoot unless a specific story or illustration explicitly requires otherwise.

---

## Foot Freckles

**Canon.**

The Kinder has a small number of freckles on his feet.

The quantity, placement, and appearance of these freckles should remain consistent with the approved Canon Reference Images.

The Kinder should have:
- No additional foot freckles
- No missing foot freckles
- No relocation of existing foot freckles

When discrepancies occur, the Canon Reference Images take precedence over newly generated artwork.

Future artwork should match the freckle placement shown in:

- Kinder_BC_Front
- Kinder_BC_Back
- Kinder_BC_Left
- Kinder_BC_Right

---

# Clothing

## Cloak

Dark olive green.

Frayed edges.

Worn but loved.

---

### Cloak Rules

The cloak is a full cloak.

Not split into tails.

Frayed edges are canon.

---

## Tunic

Brown leather adventuring clothes.

Earth tones.

---

## Pants

Greenish earth tones.

Rolled cuffs at ankles.

---

# Equipment

## Chest

### Small Chest Pouch

**Canon.**

Located on the **right side of the Kinder's chest** unless specifically instructed otherwise.

---

### Small Chest Pocket

**Canon.**

Located on the **left side of the Kinder's chest**.

This should be opposite of the Small Chest Pouch and always on the Kinder's left side unless specifically instructed otherwise.

No decoration.

---
